< review>
Really didn't want to write this review but after a number of incidents I wanted to share my thoughts. I'm new to airsoft. My teenage son was interested so we both went in in July and bought two guns, batteries, and accessories. The owner was very helpful. He explained everything, spent a lot of time answering questions, and even gave us 10% off even though the sale had already ended. But since then we've had a number of issues.

1) In August, we bought a backup battery for each gun. The salesperson sold us the wrong batteries. When we returned them (1 week later) we were charged a restocking fee even though it was their fault.

2) My son called the store to find out if they had a pistol he wanted, they confirmed it was in stock. When we arrived the salesperson was very brusque and unfriendly. He was adamant they they did not have that gun. We even asked him to check in the back since we had called. He said he was sure. Come to find out he was mistaken. This was after we drove more than 30 minutes each way. I tried to call and talk to the owner since that was really inconvenient and I wanted to ensure the gun was in stock before driving down again. He would not talk with me. When I arrived in person and bought the gun the next day, I tried to talk to him again, he refused to talk.

3) One of the original batteries I bought was used three times and then went bad. The salesperson was nice but firm. Nothing they could do. No warranty (except 7 days).

I really wanted to like this store since it is local (30 miles away). Also I always prefer to support local vendors. But after these situations, I've decided that we will use online vendors for products. Better customer service and better warranties.< /review>

< review>
Copy and pasted from my yelp review. Just trying to give this place a better review as I think they‚Äôve been doing pretty good but here it is.

I waited a couple months before doing this review for a couple reasons. Mainly to remove the bias of a single bad interaction or a single bad day on the field. Needless to say I don't think I've actually had any bad interactions or days at their field. I came in a couple times to view their merchandise and ask about certain rifles and how they compared to others, which ones they recommend and why. They gave me more information than I expected to receive. I would also call and ask a lot of questions over the phone and every time I called the other person on the phone gave me great information as well.  They aren't the biggest airsoft store I've ever been to but the staff there is very friendly and open and they do have a fairly large selection to choose from.

Playing in their cqb arena is loads of fun too. It is a little small and there are a couple areas where it feels like one side will always have an advantage over the other team but overall it is fun field to play. They have a variety of game modes they cycle through and they listen to the players when they want to play a specific one. I used their rental guns the first two times I played before bringing in my own load out. The rentals aren't too bad. Sure the rifles and magazines they give you are a little dented or scratched but they do work fine and are actually fairly accurate. They also give you knee pads, gloves, and a full face mask, basically all the essentials you need to have fun and be safe. The Refs are fairly nice and give you 5-10 minute breaks between games to gear up and get ready for the next one. Every game I've been to also had very nice players with few if any being toxic or mean.

Overall I am very impressed with Airsoft Extreme and would recommend anyone looking into starting airsoft or someone who needs to find upgrades for their gear and guns to come by and see what they have to offer.</review>

< Text>
Disclaimer: First time playing airsoft.

I really liked this place. The store personnel were very friendly and accommodating to us first timers (although some of the veterans in the store were laughing at our need to review the operations of the simple Sig pistol). The course is super small and is basically a parking lot converted into an airsoft course with makeshift barriers of barrels and plywood. It's good for quick team deathmatch rounds and the occasional capture the flag. The weekend ref (forgetting his name) and his son Bear were the highlight of our day. Both were super cool and accommodating and worked to keep the teams even and fair, while keeping things fun and informative.

Competitive prices (was shamelessly cross-shopping Amazon in the store), cool people, easy going atmosphere and noob friendly. I'd come back for sure.</Text>

<Text>Airsoft Extreme was unfriendly to me, but I must assume that if you are "in the club" then the store might have something to offer you. By that, I mean that if you are a regular at the store or know airsoft inside and out and can immediately be identified as one of their own and be accepted into the herd, then the store will likely have something to offer you. But if you are new to the game, or are thinking of learning more, this is NOT the store for you. I am completely new to airsoft, but have been paintballing and own a personal protection firearm, so I'm comfortable around gun and sporting shops. But walking into Airsoft Extreme was like walking into a comic book store in the 80s. Dark, cramped, unfriendly and with a vibe of hostility if you are perceived as an outsider.

I visited the local San Jose airsoft stores in hopes of seeing some of the guns in person and ask some questions. This was my first stop. I visited with the store with my family.

I stood near the counter, showing interest in the pistols on display and no one on staff engaged me to see if I needed help. I eventually looked around the shop a bit and returned to the case where I had to get someone's attention and ask to see a spring model. <Pictures>None</Pictures><response>None<//response><Rate>5</Rate><Review>Jack M.
0 friends 1 review
3/29/2014
Okay,
I have been to many vape shops, but not one remotely like this. The first time I came in, after grueling the worker with numerous phone calls regarding the purchase that I wanted to make, I was greeted by a respectful and cheerful employee named Kris. He was ready to help me with whatever it was that i hoped and desired, while giving me his undivided attention.

The first thing I noticed when I walked into the shop, was their HUGE selection of E-Juices that varied in flavor, size and nicotine level. Plus they let you sample whatever juice you want, to ensure satisfaction.

There is a chill ambiance in the store, that welcomes everyone 18+ from people just starting to vape to "veteran vapers." This store is also very helpful to people that are trying to quit smoking.

Another thing that's is this shop is a "vape shop." It is not a head shop that sells pipes and bongs and and other smoking accessories, this is effective because this enables them to have a vast selection of vape stuff. I appreciate the separation because this is really the way it should be. Vaping should not be associated with smoking in my opinion.

Who loves discounts, I DO! And apparently Beverly Vapes does too! There is a special discount every day with catchy names like: "TWOs Day special" and "Thirsty Thursday" (which is my favorite because it's buy 2 juices get one free!!!)

Overall I highly highly recommend this shop. People that go to any other one are really missing out.

And remember, "It's vapor not smoke." :)

(Shout out to Kris and Marylee, the best vape shop employee's ever!!!)< /Review><user_id>113892196360097594502< /user_id></record></dataset><record>

< text>
This place is OK, but just OK.  They have a fair selection of bikes and the staff are generally pleasant and knowledgeable.  Prices are fair.  Their line of Performance-branded products is all cheap stuff from China.  Gets the job done, but is certainly nothing to laud about.  I got some leg warmers with zippers that are difficult and fell apart in a matter of months anyway.  Jacket had a fastex buckle improperly attached.  I went back and checked the others to possibly exchange, but they were all like that.  Salesman explained that sometimes they get a whole run of products like that.  Service shop is reasonably quick, if lacking attention to detail.  Got a bike back that ran worse after adjustments (chain continues to fall off after gear changes).  One time I got a "complete tune-up" only to have to use the bike's air pump to fill my own tires.  I go back because they're better than Bike Attack on Main and are closer than Helen's, but if you want a higher quality shop, go to Helen's.< /text>

<text>(I wish I could post without a single star)
Terrible, worst customer service I've ever received from a bike shop. About a month ago I took in two bikes for their trade in program( to purchase a commuter bike from them) both bikes were appraised and I ended up only wanting to trade one in. They then took pictures of the bike and told me they had to send it off to see if they value was right since the wheels were different from the manufacturer, I said ok and that they would contact me within 48 hours. After 3 days I called, spoke to the manager (the assistant manager was supposed to call me back) and he told me that he himself didnt even know how the trade in program worked and would find out and call me back. Needless to say, I never received a phone call and decided to forget about it and take my business elsewhere. I sold the bike privately and took my business to Helens Cycles in Santa Monica and purchased my new commuter bike where I was helped within minutes of entering the shop. < Text>
Very helpful employees, and awesome friendly bike mechanic.  Got my first road bike from them and a bunch of over accessories over the past year.  They're also great about price matching if there's a discrepancy from their online site vs store price or if an item becomes cheaper due to some holiday sale within 30 days or something.  They've also got a very friendly return policy too.

Obviously if you're an elite cyclist, you might not find what you're looking for here, but for the 99% of the population, this bike shop should more than fill your needs.  They also have no-drop group rides on Sunday Mornings which are great for beginners/intermediate folks.

One word of caution, they sometimes get insanely busy and don't have enough staff to attend to customers.  That might be one of their weaker points during peak hours.  Otherwise, just stick to going non-peak which means, don't go on weekend afternoons.</Text>

<pics>None< /pics>< Text>
Wanted to post since it seems like people have a range of experiences here.

Been suffering from chain suck on my mtb. Called Performance and got some helpful tips and an invitation to come in whenever from Nick. Made it in, and Jorge took a look at my bike and filed down some rough metal nubs and wear on the inner part of my granny ring; he said this was what was catching and causing the suck. Gave me an ingenious way to check on a flat riding surface if chain suck was still happening (hold brakes, struggle to move forward pushing hard). Also pointed out what I'd have to buy if the suck stuck around, but without any upsell or pressure at all - actually in the context of educating me a little about my bike's gear equipment because I thought I'd need something different..

The whole thing took less than 30 minutes, and everyone was extremely helpful and friendly. I can't be certain yet whether it's resolved the issue - chain suck is complicated, and I'm trying it out on some real uphills today - but it was absolutely a positive experience and I'll be back.<//Text>

<user_id>103692951874791567679</user_id><username>ElectricStrider1</username><Date>1508986590895</Date><Rate>5<//Rate>< Text>
Dr. Marta Recasens is an absolute professional. Before I sing her praises, however, I need to provide some background regarding how I came into her care.

Roughly six months ago, I started hemorrhaging in my right eye. I soon discovered that my diabetes was out of control. Ten years of neglect had finally caught up with me. In my haste to resolve the issue, I searched online and found an ophthalmologist nearby. As it turns out, I would soon regret my decision. The ophthalmologist attempted to perform laser eye treatment without checking my blood glucose level and the result was a bruised cheek from an injection and pronounced double vision that persist to this day.

About a week later, after I had finally visited a doctor for the first time in 12 years, I was referred to Dr. Marta Recasens. I struggle to put into words how grateful I am to Dr. Recasens for all that she has done for me. Dr. Recasens immediately took charge of my case and made absolutely certain that my diabetes was under control before starting a series of eye treatments.

As I type this, I am on the road to recovery. The hemorrhaging has stopped and eyesight is clearer. The double vision caused by the other doctor has also subsided substantially. I do not subscribe to the notion of guardian angels, but Dr. Recasens comes pretty close. She is kind and gentle and absolutely no nonsense. Dr. Recasens will make certain that you know exactly what the situation with your vision is. She also has a gentle hand for the more delicate procedures.

I most highly recommend Dr. Recasens if you are looking for an ophthalmologist who is compassionate and professional. I also recommend her if you harbor any fear and anxiety regarding medical procedures. Dr. Recasens and her wonderful staff will put you at ease.
Thank you, Dr. Recasens.

- Andrew M.</Text>

In this area, Vallejo, CA, there are only two places where you can get Bahn Mi sandwiches. But I chose this one. The sandwiches are good, the service is good.  THEY NEED TO BE RECOGNIZED BETTER BECAUSE OF THEIR LOCATION.

<Text>Good Pho requires rice noodles. That is not what you will get at PHO Noodle House. They use a much thicker flour noodle which is just a mess to eat with chopsticks.

Chicken is probably a safe bet, but I would avoid the beef and pork meat choices. The Spicy Beef includes pork cuts that I've never seen in my life. They looked like half circles of bologna maybe? The beef was definitely not lean.

Nice lunch time atmosphere and service was pleasant. Although I ran into problems with the order and correcting it was a bit of a challenge.

I may go back. But I'm spoiled when it comes to Pho. Hong Kee & Kim in San Francisco is the same price and a big step up in quality. Why a Pho restaurant would use flour noodles instead of rice noodles is beyond me.< /Text>< Pictures>
None< /Pictures>

<Text>Delicious pho.

I currently work in the plaza so I frequent the restaurants pretty often. Obviously this plaza is terrible. With the homeless people and all the ricers showing off, it's not pretty. Fortunately the Vietnamese food here is actually the best in Vallejo.

Eating pho twice a week these past four years away in college, I was looking for a good Vietnamese place near home. Pho1 isn't a place to really impress anyone. Vietnamese restaurants just aren't meant for that. Instead it's a real cozy down to earth restaurant with good quality pho. I love the seafood pho they have. I hardly ever see seafood pho in Vietnamese restaurants so try it out if you like a rich garlicky seafood taste.<//Text></record></dataset><record>
< userid>
106341489896640689950< /userid>
< Name>
E A< /Name>
< Time>
1375475633888< /Time>
< rating>
4<//rating>
< Text>
PHO SHO!

Sorry, I had to get that stupid, bordering on asian teeny booper-ish misnomer out of my head before I got started on this review. Now that I have that out of the way, on to the review.

Pho (which is pronounced "fa", which also explains the phrase I mentioned at the onset of this review) is one of my favorite soups. Probably number 3 in the list of my favorite soups. My list goes like this:

1. Ramen
2. Udon
3. Pho
4. That junky oh-so bad for you Campbell's one with the mini burgers
5. Dinner cereal

Pho is awesome. Especially on a cold day where you've got a cold and your girlfriend is giving you the cold shoulder while you listen to Stone Cold Steve Austin's theme song. When you think of good quality food, you don't usually think of Vallejo, CA (aka the neglected child of the Bay Area that learned to fend for himself without parental supervision, but strictly on it's steel will and heart of frickin' GOLD.) You're... right for the most part. It's mostly fast food joints and your dime a dozen Chinese restaurants here. But here and there, peppered amongst the landscape, you'll find some good eats. Pho #1 happens to be one of those places.

This little gem is nestled nearby CVS (also the same plaza that houses Starbread aka home of the senorita sweet bread aka crack bread as well as Tapioca Express aka bored young Filipinos wanna hang out in Vallejo and OMG THIS PLACE HAS BOBA! (their wording, not mine)). It's extremely unassuming and you'd never see it driving down Sonoma Blvd. Once you drive into the plaza, you're golden. I know that Burger King is staring at you longingly, but ignore that for now. You're here for some good Vietnamese food.

Inside, the surroundings/environs aren't much to talk about. Just some very basic tables and chairs in here. It's not that big of a place either, though i've seen some pretty nice sized groups eat here before (myself being a part of one of those groups on one occassion.) You'll be handed a menu with ohhhhhhhhhhh so many things to choose from, descriptions and photos a-plenty. Ordering is done is a timely fashion as well. In a few minutes, boom, hot food is on your table.

Everything here is good. The rolls (both the rice noodle ones and fried) are a great way to start a meal here. Just the right amount of tasty nomage. The rice plates are pretty much the bomb. My favorite rice plate is the standard BBQ pork with the egg. I always order an extra egg as I LOVE FRIED EGGS. And there is just wayyy too many good soups to choose from. My favorite would probably be the beef combination one with the beef ball, steak, flank, and tripe. Chicken and seafood soups are also no slouches here. The flavors here are always off the wall and you always get large hearty portions. Leaving here hungry means either a) you didn't order food or b) you are, in fact, the cyborgs that the Conner family tried to warm me about. That and something about a Skynet.

If you're in Vallejo for some reason or another (I can only assume you have family here OR you're visiting Six Flags) and you're craving some really good Vietnamese food, do yourself a huge favor and go to Pho #1. You will leave full and satisfied, the top two things on your meal experience list... which goes like this:

1. Full
2. Satisfied
3. Ice water
4. Man at nearby table keeps giving me disturbing/awesome look
5. Dinner cereal</Text>
